ENTRY            E1842   20040311                             0000E184200000001 
SUBENT        E1842001   20040311                             0000E184200100001 
BIB                 14         56                                 E184200100002 
TITLE      Preequilibrium (p,p') spectra for nuclei around        E184200100003 
           neutron number 50                                      E184200100004 
AUTHOR     (Y.Watanabe, I.Kumabe, M.Hyakutake, N.Koori, K.Ogawa,  E184200100005 
           K.Orito, K.Akagi, N.Oda)                               E184200100006 
INSTITUTE  (2JPNKYU)Department of Nuclear Engineering             E184200100007 
REFERENCE  (J,PR/C,36,(4),1325,198710)                            E184200100008 
REL-REF    (R,E1303001,I.Kumabe+,J,PR/C,35,(2),467,198702)        E184200100009 
           Detailed information on targets                        E184200100010 
PART-DET   (P)                                                    E184200100011 
SAMPLE     - Target is natural.                                   E184200100012 
           - Chemical-form of target is element.                  E184200100013 
           - Physical-form of target is solid.                    E184200100014 
           - Target-thickness is 0.5 to 1 mg/cm**2. Detailed      E184200100015 
             information on the target is listed in Table I of    E184200100016 
             [I.Kumabe et al., Phys. Rev. C35 (1987) 467].        E184200100017 
           - Target is self supported.                            E184200100018 
METHOD     (BCINT)Beam intensity was determined with a current    E184200100019 
                  integrator connected to a Faraday cup and was   E184200100020 
                  also monitored by a detector located at a fixed E184200100021 
                  backward angle to the beam.                     E184200100022 
           (EDE)Signals of protons were separated from those of   E184200100023 
                other charged particles with a particle           E184200100024 
                identification circuit.                           E184200100025 
FACILITY   (VDGT,2JPNKYU)                                         E184200100026 
DETECTOR   (SIBAR)Used as Delta E counter, 75 micro-meter         E184200100027 
           (SILI)Used as E counter, 2500 micro-meter              E184200100028 
CORRECTION Two kinds of backgrounds were carefully subtracted in  E184200100029 
           the data processing. One is the continuous background  E184200100030 
           due to the slit scattering of elastic protons by the   E184200100031 
           detector aperture. It was estimated under the          E184200100032 
           assumption that the 30 deg spectrum measured using a   E184200100033 
           gold target could be attributed to the degraded        E184200100034 
           elastic protons. The other component of background     E184200100035 
           consisted of discrete peaks due to light-element       E184200100036 
           impurities on the targets, such as hydrogen, carbon,   E184200100037 
           and oxygen. After these peaks were identified in the   E184200100038 
           measured spectra, they were subtracted by drawing a    E184200100039 
           curve under the peak on the assumption that the        E184200100040 
           spectrum must be smooth in the continuum region.       E184200100041 
ERR-ANALYS Uncertainties associated with the normalization was    E184200100042 
           estimated to be within 10% for each target. However,   E184200100043 
           the relative uncertainties of the cross sections for   E184200100044 
           different targets is believed to be less than 4%.      E184200100045 
COMMENT    Absolute cross sections were determined by normalizing E184200100046 
           the experimental elastic cross sections to the optical E184200100047 
           model predictions at forward angles. The normalization E184200100048 
           factors for two sets of global optical model           E184200100049 
           parameters were compared in order to estimate the      E184200100050 
           uncertainties involved in this method. Optical model   E184200100051 
           parameter [F.D. Becchetti, Jr. and G.W. Greenlees,     E184200100052 
           Phys. Rev. 182(1969)1190] were adopted.                E184200100053 
HISTORY    (20030716T)Data converted from NRDF D1320 and EXFOR    E184200100054 
                      O0504. Numerical data are exchanged with    E184200100055 
                      author's one and data which are obtained in E184200100056 
                      the same work but not shown in the original E184200100057 
                      reference are added.                        E184200100058
